Because the 'any' value of an empty iterable in Python is False we\n        # can start with an array full of zeros and set to one only if any\n        # value encountered is True\n        flag_val = 1\n    else:\n        raise ValueError(\"'val_test' must be either 'any' or 'all'!\")\n\n    out[:] = 1 - flag_val\n\n    with nogil:\n        for i in range(N):\n            lab = labels[i]\n            if lab < 0:\n                continue\n\n            for j in range(K):\n                if skipna and mask[i, j]:\n                    continue\n\n                if uses_mask and mask[i, j]:\n                    # We cannot use util.is_nan\n                            # because of no gil\n                            compensation[lab, j] = 0\n\n                        # Handle complex overflow\n compensation[lab, j].real = 0\n\n                        if (\n                            sum_t is complex64_t or sum_t is complex128_t\n                        ) and not isfinite(compensation[lab, j].imag):\n                            compensation[lab, j].imag = 0\n\n                        sumx[lab, j] = t\n                elif not skipna:\n                    if uses_mask:\n min_count, sumx\n    )\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\ndef group_prod(\n    int64float_t[:, ::1] out,\n    int64_t[::1] counts,\n    ndarray[int64float_t, ndim=2] values,\n ddof)\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\n@cython.cdivision(True)\n@cython.cpow(True)\ndef group_skew(\n    float64_t[:, ::1] out,\n    int64_t[::1] counts,\n    ndarray[float64_t, ndim=2] values,\n    const intp_t[::1] labels,\n    const uint8_t[:, :] mask=None,\n    uint8_t[:, ::1] result_mask=None,\n    bint skipna=True,\n) -> None:\n    cdef:\n        Py_ssize_t i, j, N, K, lab, ngroups = len(counts)\n        int64_t[:, ::1] nobs\n        Py_ssize_t len_values = len(values), len_labels = len(labels)\n        bint isna_entry, uses_mask = mask is not None\n        float64_t[:, ::1] M1, M2, M3\n        float64_t delta, delta_n, term1, val\n        int64_t n1, n\n        float64_t ct\n\n    if len_values != len_labels:\n        raise ValueError(\"len(index) != len(labels)\")\n\n    nobs = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.int64)\n\n    # M1, M2, and M3 correspond to 1st, 2nd, and third Moments\n    M1 = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.float64)\n    M2 = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.float64)\n    M3 = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    N, K = (<object>values).shape\n\n    out[:, :] = 0.0\n\n    with nogil:\n        for i in range(N):\n            lab = labels[i]\n            if lab < 0:\n                continue\n\n            counts[lab] += 1\n\n            for j in range(K):\n                val = values[i, j]\n\n                if uses_mask:\n                    isna_entry = mask[i, j]\n                else:\n                    isna_entry = _treat_as_na(val, False)\n\n                if not isna_entry:\n                    # Running stats update based on RunningStats::Push from\n                    #  https://www.johndcook.com/blog/skewness_kurtosis/\n                    n1 = nobs[lab, j]\n                    n = n1 + 1\n\n                    nobs[lab, j] = n\n                    delta = val - M1[lab, j]\n                    delta_n = delta / n\n                    term1 = delta * delta_n * n1\n\n                    M1[lab, j] += delta_n\n                    M3[lab, j] += term1 * delta_n * (n - 2) - 3 * delta_n * M2[lab, j]\n                    M2[lab, j] += term1\n                elif not skipna:\n                    M1[lab, j] = NaN\n                    M2[lab, j] = NaN\n                    M3[lab, j] = NaN\n\n        for i in range(ngroups):\n            for j in range(K):\n                ct = <float64_t>nobs[i, j]\n                if ct < 3:\n                    if result_mask is not None:\n                        result_mask[i, j] = 1\n                    out[i, j] = NaN\n                elif M2[i, j] == 0:\n                    out[i, j] = 0\n                else:\n                    out[i, j] = (\n                        (ct * (ct - 1) ** 0.5 / (ct - 2))\n                        * (M3[i, j] / M2[i, j] ** 1.5)\n                    )\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\n@cython.cdivision(True)\n@cython.cpow(True)\ndef group_kurt(\n    float64_t[:, ::1] out,\n    int64_t[::1] counts,\n    ndarray[float64_t, ndim=2] values,\n    const intp_t[::1] labels,\n    const uint8_t[:, :] mask=None,\n    uint8_t[:, ::1] result_mask=None,\n    bint skipna=True,\n) -> None:\n    cdef:\n        Py_ssize_t i, j, N, K, lab, ngroups = len(counts)\n        int64_t[:, ::1] nobs\n        Py_ssize_t len_values = len(values), len_labels = len(labels)\n        bint isna_entry, uses_mask = mask is not None\n        float64_t[:, ::1] M1, M2, M3, M4\n        float64_t delta, delta_n, delta_n2, term1, val\n        int64_t n1, n\n        float64_t ct, num, den, adj\n\n    if len_values != len_labels:\n        raise ValueError(\"len(index) != len(labels)\")\n\n    nobs = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.int64)\n\n    # M1, M2, M3 and M4 correspond to 1st, 2nd, 3rd and 4th Moments\n    M1 = np.zeros((<object>out).shape, dtype=np.float64)\n\n    N, K = (<object>values).shape\n\n    out[:, :] = 0.0\n\n    with nogil:\n        for i in range(N):\n            lab = labels[i]\n            if isna_entry = mask[i, j]\n                else:\n                    isna_entry = _treat_as_na(val, False)\n\n                if not isna_entry:\n                    # Running stats update based on RunningStats::Push from\n                    #  https://www.johndcook.com/blog/skewness_kurtosis/\n                    n1 = nobs[lab, j]\n                    n = n1 + 1\n\n                    nobs[lab, j] = n\n                    delta = val - M1[lab, j]\n                    delta_n = delta / n\n                    delta_n2 = delta_n * delta_n\n                    term1 = delta * delta_n * n1\n\n                    M1[lab, j] += delta_n\n                    M4[lab, j] += (term1 * delta_n2 * (n*n - 3*n + 3)\n                                   + 6 * delta_n2 * M2[lab, j]\n                                   - 4 * delta_n * M3[lab, j])\n                    M3[lab, j] += term1 * delta_n * (n - 2) - 3 * delta_n * M2[lab, j]\n                    M2[lab, j] += term1\n                elif not skipna:\n                    M1[lab, j] = NaN\n                    M2[lab, j] = NaN\n                    M3[lab, j] = NaN\n                    M4[lab, j] = NaN\n\n        for i in range(ngroups):\n            for j in range(K):\n                ct = <float64_t>nobs[i, j]\n                if ct < 4:\n                    if result_mask is not None:\n                        result_mask[i, j] = 1\n          den = (ct - 2) * (ct - 3) * M2[i, j] ** 2\n                    adj = 3.0 * (ct - 1) ** 2 / ((ct - 2) * (ct - 3))\n                    out[i, j] = num / den - adj\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\ndef group_mean(\n    mean_t[:, ::1] out,\n    int64_t[::1] counts,\n    ndarray[mean_t, ndim=2] values,\n    const intp_t[::1] labels,\n float64_t[:, ::1] out,\n    ndarray[numeric_t, ndim=1] values,\n    const intp_t[::1] labels,\n    const uint8_t[:] mask,\n    const float64_t[:] qs,\n    const int64_t[::1] starts,\n    const ----------\n    out : np.ndarray[np.float64, ndim=2]\n        Array of aggregated values that will be written to.\n    values : np.ndarray\n        Array containing the values to apply the function  Positions at which each group begins.\n    ends : ndarray[int64]\n        Positions at which each group ends.\n    interpolation : {'linear', 'lower', 'highest', 'nearest', 'midpoint'}\n src=\"https://colab.research.google.com/assets/colab-badge.svg\" alt=\"Open In Colab\"/></a>         |\n# PDEP-6: Ban upcasting in setitem-like operations\n\n- Created: 23 December 2022\n- Status: Implemented\n- Discussion: [#50424](https://github.com/pandas-dev/pandas/pull/50424)\n- Author: [Marco Gorelli](https://github.com/MarcoGorelli) ([original issue](https://github.com/pandas-dev/pandas/issues/39584) by [Joris Van den Bossche](https://github.com/jorisvandenbossche))\n- Revision: 1\n\n[TOC]\n\n## Abstract\n\nThe suggestion is that setitem-like operations would\nnot change a ``Series``' dtype (nor that of a ``DataFrame``'s column).\n\nCurrent behaviour:\n```python\nIn [1]: ser = pd.Series([1, 2, 3], dtype='int64')\n\nIn [2]: ser[2] = 'potage'\n\nIn [3]: ser  # dtype changed to 'object'!\nOut[3]:\n0         1\n1         2\n2    potage\ndtype: object\n```\n\nSuggested behaviour:\n\n```python\nIn [1]: ser = pd.Series([1, 2, 3])\n\nIn [2]: ser[2] = 'potage'  # raises!\n---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nValueError: Invalid value 'potage' for dtype int64\n```\n\n## Motivation and Scope\n\nCurrently, pandas is extremely flexible in handling different dtypes.\nHowever, this can potentially hide bugs, break user expectations, and copy data\nin what looks like it should be an inplace operation.\n\nAn example of it hiding a bug is:\n```python\nIn[9]: ser = pd.Series(pd.date_range(\"2000\", periods=3))\n\nIn[10]: ser[2] = \"2000-01-04\"  # works, is converted to datetime64\n\nIn[11]: ser[2] = \"2000-01-04x\"  # typo - but pandas does not error, it upcasts to object\n```\n\nThe scope of this PDEP is limited to setitem-like operations on Series (and DataFrame columns).\nFor example, starting with:\n```python\ndf = DataFrame({\"a\": [1, 2, np.nan], \"b\": [4, 5, 6]})\nser = df[\"a\"].copy()\n```\nthen the following would all raise:\n\n* setitem-like operations:\n\n    - ``ser.fillna('foo', inplace=True)``\n    - ``ser.where(ser.isna(), 'foo', inplace=True)``\n    - ``ser.fillna('foo', inplace=False)``\n    - ``ser.where(ser.isna(), 'foo', inplace=False)``\n\n* setitem indexing operations (where ``indexer`` could be a slice, a mask,\n  a single value, a list or array of values, or any other allowed indexer):","is_error":false}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dc69f8e0-e60b-493e-8756-b9d038abd81e","uuid":"2eced33b-a9d6-4ad7-9542-f8f9aa7a9bae","tool_use_result":{"stdout":"sphinxext\n=========\n\nThis directory contains custom sphinx extensions in use in the pandas\ndocumentation.\n# Pandas Cheat Sheet\n\nThe Pandas Cheat Sheet was created using Microsoft Powerpoint 2013.\nTo create the PDF version, within Powerpoint, simply do a \"Save As\"\nand pick \"PDF\" as the format.\n\nThis cheat sheet, originally written by Irv Lustig, [Princeton src=\"https://colab.research.google.com/assets/colab-badge.svg\" alt=\"Open In Colab\"/></a>         |\n# PDEP-6: Ban upcasting in setitem-like operations\n\n- Created: 23 December 2022\n- Status: Implemented\n- Discussion: [#50424](https://github.com/pandas-dev/pandas/pull/50424)\n- Author: [Marco Gorelli](https://github.com/MarcoGorelli) ([original issue](https://github.com/pandas-dev/pandas/issues/39584) by [Joris Van den Bossche](https://github.com/jorisvandenbossche))\n- Revision: 1\n\n[TOC]\n\n## Abstract\n\nThe suggestion is that setitem-like operations would\nnot change a ``Series``' dtype (nor that of a ``DataFrame``'s column).\n\nCurrent behaviour:\n```python\nIn [1]: ser = pd.Series([1, 2, 3], dtype='int64')\n\nIn [2]: ser[2] = 'potage'\n\nIn [3]: ser  # dtype changed to 'object'!\nOut[3]:\n0         1\n1         2\n2    potage\ndtype: object\n```\n\nSuggested behaviour:\n\n```python\nIn [1]: ser = pd.Series([1, 2, 3])\n\nIn [2]: ser[2] = 'potage'  # raises!\n---------------------------------------------------------------------------\nValueError: Invalid value 'potage' for dtype int64\n```\n\n## Motivation and Scope\n\nCurrently, pandas is extremely flexible in handling different dtypes.\nHowever, this can potentially hide bugs, break user expectations, and copy data\nin what looks like it should be an inplace operation.\n\nAn example of it hiding a bug is:\n```python\nIn[9]: ser = pd.Series(pd.date_range(\"2000\", periods=3))\n\nIn[10]: ser[2] = \"2000-01-04\"  # works, is converted to datetime64\n\nIn[11]: ser[2] = \"2000-01-04x\"  # typo - but pandas does not error, it upcasts to object\n```\n\nThe scope of this PDEP is limited to setitem-like operations on Series (and DataFrame columns).\nFor example, starting with:\n```python\ndf = DataFrame({\"a\": [1, 2, np.nan], \"b\": [4, 5, 6]})\nser = df[\"a\"].copy()\n```\nthen the following would all raise:\n\n* setitem-like operations:\n\n    - ``ser.fillna('foo', inplace=True)``\n    - ``ser.where(ser.isna(), 'foo', inplace=True)``\n    - ``ser.fillna('foo', inplace=False)``\n    - ``ser.where(ser.isna(), 'foo', inplace=False)``\n\n* setitem indexing operations (where ``indexer`` could be a slice, a mask,\n  a single value, a list or array of values, or any other allowed indexer):","stderr":"","interrupted":false,"isImage":false,"noOutputExpected":false}}

If a function, must either\n   328→            work when passed a Series or when passed to Series.apply.\n   329→\n   330→            Accepted combinations are:\n   331→\n   332→            - function\n   333→            - string function name\n   334→            - list of functions and/or function names, e.g. ``[np.sum, 'mean']``\n   335→            - None, in which case ``**kwargs`` are used with Named Aggregation. Here\n   336→              the output has one column for each element in ``**kwargs``. The name of\n   337→              the column is keyword, whereas the value determines the aggregation\n   338→              used to compute the values in the column.\n   339→\n   340→              Can also accept a Numba JIT function with\n   341→              ``engine='numba'`` specified. Only passing a single function is supported\n   342→              with this engine.\n   343→\n   344→              If the ``'numba'`` engine is chosen, the function must be\n   345→              a user defined function with ``values`` and ``index`` as the\n   346→              first and second arguments respectively in the function signature.\n   347→              Each group's index will be passed to the user defined function\n   348→              and optionally available for use.\n   349→\n   350→        *args\n   351→            Positional arguments to pass to func.\n   352→        engine : str, default None\n   353→            * ``'cython'`` : Runs the function through C-extensions from cython.\n   354→            * ``'numba'`` : Runs the function through JIT compiled code from numba.\n   355→            * ``None`` : Defaults to ``'cython'`` or globally setting\n   356→                ``compute.use_numba``\n   357→\n   358→        engine_kwargs : dict, default None\n   359→            * For ``'cython'`` engine, there are no accepted ``engine_kwargs``\n   360→            * For ``'numba'`` engine, the engine can accept ``nopython``, ``nogil``\n   361→              and ``parallel`` dictionary keys. The values must either be ``True`` or\n   362→              ``False``. Using numpy's advanced indexing instead of group splitting\n+        2. Avoiding expensive data splitter creation\n+        3. Using fast numpy.take() for indexing\n+        4. Minimizing Python object creation in tight loops\n+        \"\"\"\n+        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype=\"O\")\n+        initialized = False\n+\n+        codes_list = self.codes\n+\n+        # Single level grouping path - optimized for the common case\n+        if len(codes_list) == 1:\n+            codes = codes_list[0]\n+            ngroups = self.ngroups\n+            # Use numpy's where() to find indices matching each code value\n+            # This is more cache-efficient than the splitter approach\n+            for group_id in range(ngroups):\n+                # Find all indices where code equals group_id\n+                # np.where is highly optimized and uses fast C code\n+                indices = np.where(codes == group_id)[0]\n+\n+                if len(indices) > 0:\n+                    # Use take() which is faster than iloc for many indices\n+                    group = obj.take(indices)\n+                    res = func(group)\n+                    res = extract_result(res)\n+\n+                    if not initialized:\n+                        check_result_array(res, obj.dtype)\n+                        initialized = True\n+\n+                    result[group_id] = res\n+        else:\n+            # Multi-level grouping uses original approach\n+            return self._aggregate_series_pure_python(obj, func)\n+\n+        return result\n\n     @final\n     def _aggregate_series_pure_python(\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":474,"cache_read_input_tokens":81641,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":474},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dc69f8e0-e60b-493e-8756-b9d038abd81e","uuid":"6b6e1717-9365-4bf6-842d-3ee77dc21954"}

Minimizing Python object creation in tight loops\n+        \"\"\"\n+        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype=\"O\")\n+        initialized = False\n+\n+        codes_list = self.codes\n+\n+        # Single level grouping path - optimized for the common case\n+        if len(codes_list) == 1:\n+            codes = codes_list[0]\n+            ngroups = self.ngroups\n+            # Use numpy's where() to find indices matching each code value\n+            # This is more cache-efficient than the splitter approach\n+            for group_id in range(ngroups):\n+                # Find all indices where code equals group_id\n+                # np.where is highly optimized and uses fast C code\n+                indices = np.where(codes == group_id)[0]\n+\n+                if len(indices) > 0:\n+                    # Use take() which is faster than iloc for many indices\n+                    group = obj.take(indices)\n+                    res = func(group)\n+                    res = extract_result(res)\n+\n+                    if not initialized:\n+                        check_result_array(res, obj.dtype)\n+                        initialized = True\n+\n+                    result[group_id] = res\n+        else:\n+            # Multi-level grouping uses original approach\n+            return self._aggregate_series_pure_python(obj, func)\n+\n+        return result\n\n     @final\n     def apply_groupwise(\n"}}

Minimizing Python object creation in tight loops\n+        \"\"\"\n+        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype=\"O\")\n+        initialized = False\n+\n+        codes_list = self.codes\n+\n+        # Single level grouping path -
